<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Handball_European_Championship_2012_-_en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="520" data-file-width="680" height="229" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Handball_European_Championship_2012_-_en.svg/300px-Handball_European_Championship_2012_-_en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Handball_European_Championship_2012_-_en.svg/450px-Handball_European_Championship_2012_-_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Handball_European_Championship_2012_-_en.svg/600px-Handball_European_Championship_2012_-_en.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Handball_European_Championship_2012_-_en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Countries that qualified for the championship</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <b>2012 EHF <a href="/wiki/European_Men%27s_Handball_Championship" title="European Men's Handball Championship">European Men's Handball Championship</a></b> was the tenth edition of the men's continental <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Team_handball" title="Team handball">handball</a> tournament, which was held in <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> between 15–29 January 2012. Sixteen teams qualified for the event, including host nation Serbia, defending champion France and fourteen national teams through the qualifying tournament. The teams were split into four groups of 4, with the top 3 teams of each group advancing to the main round, carrying the points won against other qualified opponents. Going to the main round with no points, <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_handball_team" title="Denmark national handball team">Denmark</a> ended up winning the championship after defeating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbia_national_handball_team" title="Serbia national handball team">Serbia</a> in the final with a scoreline of 21–19.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-denmarkgold_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-denmarkgold-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The bronze medal was claimed by Croatia, who defeated Spain 31-27 to win their second bronze and fourth European medal overall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> In the placement match for the 5th position Macedonia proved to be too strong for Slovenia and won the match by 28–27. Macedonian right back <a href="/wiki/Kiril_Lazarov" title="Kiril Lazarov">Kiril Lazarov</a> led his team with 8 goals to success and took the top scorers' award with a European Championship record of 61 goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Over 300,000 spectators were present in 47 matches during the tournament, which was also a new championship record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-denmarkgold_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-denmarkgold-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>By winning the European title, Denmark directly qualified for the <a href="/wiki/Handball_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Handball at the 2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a>, while Serbia and Macedonia secured a spot in the <a href="/wiki/Handball_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_qualification" title="Handball at the 2012 Summer Olympics – Men's qualification">Olympic Qualification Tournament</a>. Thanks to the Danish triumph, Poland also made it to the qualifiers as the eighth ranked team of the 2011 World Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The championship was somewhat overshadowed by incidents that occurred during the final week of the event. On 26–27 January, in violent attacks, cars were damaged or set on fire, and several Croatian supporters were injured. In the semifinal match between Serbia and Croatia, <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDarko_%C5%A0e%C5%A1um" title="Žarko Šešum">Žarko Šešum</a>, the back player of the Serbian team had his eye severely injured after a bottle intended for Croatian player <a href="/wiki/Ivano_Bali%C4%87" title="Ivano Balić">Ivano Balić</a> and coach <a href="/wiki/Slavko_Golu%C5%BEa" title="Slavko Goluža">Slavko Goluža</a> was thrown at him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012_European_Men%27s_Handball_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The EHF decided that Serbia would host the tournament in the cities of <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ni%C5%A1" title="Niš">Niš</a>, <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad" title="Novi Sad">Novi Sad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vr%C5%A1ac" title="Vršac">Vršac</a>. <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> were the other applicants for the championship.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Qualification">Qualification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012_European_Men%27s_Handball_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Qualification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2012_European_Men%27s_Handball_Championship_qualification" title="2012 European Men's Handball Championship qualification">2012 European Men's Handball Championship qualification</a></div>
<p>The 2012 Championship was the second for which the <a href="/wiki/2010_European_Men%27s_Handball_Championship_qualification#Qualification_system" title="2010 European Men's Handball Championship qualification">new qualification system</a> was used.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seeding">Seeding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012_European_Men%27s_Handball_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Seeding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The draw was held on 15 June 2011 in <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> at 12:00 local time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The seeding was announced on 13 June 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_stage">Group stage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012_European_Men%27s_Handball_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Group stage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The match schedule was released and confirmed on 18 April 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Four teams were selected to play in the four venue cities, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbia_national_handball_team" title="Serbia national handball team">Serbia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_national_handball_team" title="Macedonia national handball team">Macedonia</a> at <a href="/wiki/Ni%C5%A1" title="Niš">Niš</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary_national_handball_team" title="Hungary national handball team">Hungary</a> at <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad" title="Novi Sad">Novi Sad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Croatia_national_handball_team" title="Croatia national handball team">Croatia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vr%C5%A1ac" title="Vršac">Vršac</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The playing schedule was announced on 1 July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>All times are <a href="/wiki/Central_European_Time" title="Central European Time">UTC+1</a>.</i></p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<td style="background:#ccffcc;">    </td>
<td>Team advanced to the Main Round</td>
</tr>
</table>

<p>(A) and (B) indicates from which group the teams came; in the main round they were only playing against teams from the other group. By three victories and the misfortune of among others Germany, Denmark qualified for the semifinals together with the host, Serbia. Notable results were Denmarks last seconds win against Macedonia and Polands turn-around of first half result 9-20 to win second half by the same ciffres thereby equalizing against Sweden.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Final">Final</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012_European_Men%27s_Handball_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Final">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table cellspacing="0" style="width: 100%; background-color: gold">
<tr>
<td rowspan="4" style="vertical-align:top;text-align:right;" width="15%">29 January 2012<br/>
17:00</td>
<td style="vertical-align:top;text-align:right;" width="24%"><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbia_national_handball_team" title="Serbia national handball team">Serbia</a><span class="flagicon"> <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1350" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Flag_of_Serbia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Serbia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Flag_of_Serbia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Serbia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Flag_of_Serbia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Serbia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></span></b></td>
<td style="vertical-align:top;text-align:center;" width="13%"><b>19–21</b></td>
<td style="vertical-align:top;" width="24%"><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="280" data-file-width="370" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Denmark.svg/20px-Flag_of_Denmark.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Denmark.svg/31px-Flag_of_Denmark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Denmark.svg/40px-Flag_of_Denmark.svg.png 2x" width="20"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_handball_team" title="Denmark national handball team">Denmark</a></b></td>

</table>
<p>The final was played at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belgrade_Arena" title="Belgrade Arena">Belgrade Arena</a> between the host-nation <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbia_national_handball_team" title="Serbia national handball team">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_handball_team" title="Denmark national handball team">Denmark</a>, and was seen by 19,800 spectators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The teams played a match against each other in the group stage of the tournament, when Serbia defeated Denmark 24–22. Serbia's coach <a href="/wiki/Veselin_Vukovi%C4%87" title="Veselin Vuković">Veselin Vuković</a> could not rely on <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDarko_%C5%A0e%C5%A1um" title="Žarko Šešum">Žarko Šešum</a>, whose left eye was injured after he was hit with a bottle on the halftime break of the semi-final match against <a href="/wiki/Croatia_national_handball_team" title="Croatia national handball team">Croatia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The match started with tough play by both teams and low scoring. Denmark claimed the lead in the early phase of the match and controlled the period. Serbia's attacks were ineffective, and goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Darko_Stani%C4%87" title="Darko Stanić">Darko Stanić</a> made several saves. The Danes made fewer mistakes in the attacks and <a href="/wiki/Anders_Eggert" title="Anders Eggert">Anders Eggert</a> scored important goals in the counter-attacks. Denmark led at halftime 9–7.</p>
<p>Early in the second half Denmark took an 11–7 lead, but then the Serbian players halted the opponent's run with a better play in defence, except for <a href="/wiki/Mikkel_Hansen" title="Mikkel Hansen">Mikkel Hansen</a> who scored with his powerful shots in the critical moments of the game. The Danes were having the lead all the time with a margin of 1–4 goals and thanks to the saves of their goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Niklas_Landin_Jacobsen" title="Niklas Landin Jacobsen">Niklas Landin Jacobsen</a> prevented the Serbians to level the result. The last minutes of the game were played with many mistakes on both sides, but Hansen scored the decisive goal for peerless lead 21–18 with 20 seconds to go. Serbia scored until the end making it 21–19 in favor of Denmark at the end. This was the second title for Denmark after they have previously won the European Championship in <a href="/wiki/2008_European_Men%27s_Handball_Championship" title="2008 European Men's Handball Championship">2008</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-denmarkgold_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-denmarkgold-1">[1]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents">Incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012_European_Men%27s_Handball_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Riots">Riots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012_European_Men%27s_Handball_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Riots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 24 January 2012, after the match between Croatia and France, Serbian hooligans attacked Croatian fans in several locations in <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a>, northern <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad" title="Novi Sad">Novi Sad</a>, Croatian supporters were heading home after the game, when they ran into a road block and some 50 masked men assaulted them with stones, bricks and axes, smashing windscreens. The attack left several supporters injured and one of them hospitalized. In <a href="/wiki/Ruma" title="Ruma">Ruma</a>, about 30 kilometres (19 mi) south from Novi Sad, a Croatian van was set on fire and one of the passengers stabbed with a knife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>A day later the unrest continued and many cars were damaged, torched, or burnt out throughout Novi Sad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The Croatian Foreign Ministry officially complained to Serbian Ambassador Stanimir Vukicevic over the attacks; Vukicevic expressed regret and stated that the Serbian police was already taking the necessary steps. Thirteen people were arrested in connection with the incident, including Ivan Ključovski and Jovan Bajić, leaders of a fan group from Novi Sad, and a member of the <a href="/wiki/Obraz_(organization)" title="Obraz (organization)">Obraz</a> right-wing organization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> After questioning, all of them remained in custody for a month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Serbia.E2.80.93Croatia_semifinal">Serbia–Croatia semifinal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012_European_Men%27s_Handball_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Serbia–Croatia semifinal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Serbia and Croatia met in the semi-final of the tournament, which caused further concern on both sides. About 5,000 policemen were deployed to ensure the security of the fans, while in Croatia some tourist agencies cancelled trips for the match and the <a href="/wiki/Croatian_Handball_Federation" title="Croatian Handball Federation">Croatian Handball Federation</a> (Hrvatski rukometni savez, HRS) also recommended not to go to Serbia as the supporters' safety might not be guaranteed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera-23">[23]</a></sup> Spokesman Zlatko Skrinjar also added that the HRS had planned to organize trips for the event, however, they changed their mind due to the incidents in the preceding days. On the Croatian-Serbian border, joint checkpoints were set up to prevent hooligans and other groups who have no ticket for the match to enter Serbia, and to escort the fans with tickets from the border to Belgrade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>The police reported that there were no incidents during the match,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> which was eventually won by the Serbians 26–22, however, a bottle actually meant for Croatian playmaker <a href="/wiki/Ivano_Bali%C4%87" title="Ivano Balić">Ivano Balić</a> and coach <a href="/wiki/Slavko_Golu%C5%BEa" title="Slavko Goluža">Slavko Goluža</a> hit Serbian back player <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDarko_%C5%A0e%C5%A1um" title="Žarko Šešum">Žarko Šešum</a>, severely injuring his eye.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Šešum's eye suffered significant bleeding. After the trauma he had only minimal vision on the affected eye, but the risk of permanent sight loss was reportedly averted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Morten Stig Christensen, Secretary of the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Handball_Federation" title="Danish Handball Federation">Danish Handball Federation</a>, Serbia's opponent in the final said that he was "severely shocked" by the incident and so were the people from the <a href="/wiki/European_Handball_Federation" title="European Handball Federation">European Handball Federation</a> with whom he spoke. Christensen also added that he was shocked that although there were more than five thousand security personnel at the stadium, the hooligans still managed to sneak in Roman candles and laser lights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
